2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`

5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
```

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)

4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Prometheus Metrics Exposition Pattern Across Kubernetes and Grafana

## Your Task

Find the Go source files in both kubernetes/kubernetes and grafana/grafana that implement the Prometheus metrics exposition pattern: where metrics are registered using the Prometheus client_golang library, how metric collectors are organized, and where the `/metrics` HTTP endpoint is configured to expose them. Compare how both projects structure their metrics infrastructure.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain. Both Kubernetes and Grafana use the Prometheus client_golang library to expose internal metrics, but they organize their metrics registration and exposition differently. Your goal is to map these patterns across both codebases.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/grafana--v11.4.0.


## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?
- **Symbol identification**: Correct symbol names and locations?
- **Keyword presence**: Did you mention key concepts (metrics registry, collectors, exposition)?

68-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the Prometheus metrics exposition patterns in both Kubernetes and Grafana. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

### **Kubernetes (v1.32.0) - Sophisticated, Version-Aware Pattern**
- Uses a custom `KubeRegistry` interface with stability-level tracking and deprecation management
- Metrics registered via `Register()` functions in individual subsystems (API server, etcd3, flow control, etc.)
- Global `legacyregistry` provides centralized collection with automatic process/Go runtime metrics
- HTTP endpoints: `/metrics` (main) and `/metrics/slis` (SLI-specific)
- Complex `StableCollector` interface for managing metric visibility based on version
- Designed for long-term API stability with hidden metrics and deprecation warnings

### **Grafana (v11.4.0) - Simplified, Application-Centric Pattern**
- All metrics declared as global variables initialized in `init()` blocks
- Single `initMetricVars()` function registers all metrics via `MustRegister()`
- Separate HTTP service (`instrumentationService`) running on dedicated port
- Single `/metrics` endpoint using standard `promhttp.Handler()`
- Automatic "grafana_" prefix wrapper applied to all metrics
- Uses Google `wire` framework for dependency injection
- Reuses Kubernetes' `legacyregistry` internally but adds custom wrapping

### **Exposition Endpoints**
- **Kubernetes**: Multiple routes with custom instrumentation
- **Grafana**: Simple direct `promhttp.Handler()` in isolated service

The answer.json file contains 13 key files, 32 important symbols, and a detailed narrative explaining how both projects structure their metrics infrastructure with specific focus on collector organization, registration patterns, and HTTP endpoint configuration.

Metrics Exposition Pattern: Kubernetes vs Grafana\\n\\n### Overview\\nBoth Kubernetes (v1.32.0) and Grafana (v11.4.0) use the Prometheus client_golang library to expose internal metrics. However, they implement significantly different architectural patterns for metric registration, collection, and exposition.\\n\\n### Kubernetes Metrics Infrastructure\\n\\n**Architecture Pattern:** Kubernetes uses a hierarchical, stability-aware metrics registry system designed for long-term metric versioning and deprecation management.\\n\\n**Core Components:**\\n\\n1. **Registry Implementation** (`staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/registry.go`):\\n   - `KubeRegistry` interface defines the contract for metric registration and collection\\n   - `kubeRegistry` struct wraps Prometheus registries with version-awareness and deprecation tracking\\n   - Supports `Register()` and `MustRegister()` methods that check metric stability levels\\n   - Implements `Registerable` interface for collectors that support version-aware registration\\n   - Tracks hidden and disabled metrics separately via `hiddenCollectors` and `disabledMetrics` maps\\n\\n2. **Legacy Registry Pattern** (`staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/legacyregistry/registry.go`):\\n   - Provides a global `defaultRegistry` instance that all components use\\n   - `Handler()` returns an HTTP handler instrumented via `promhttp.InstrumentMetricHandler()` and `promhttp.HandlerFor()`\\n   - Automatically registers process and Go runtime collectors via `collectors.NewProcessCollector()` and `collectors.NewGoCollector()`\\n   - `HandlerWithReset()` variant supports DELETE method for test-driven metric resets\\n\\n3. **Collector Framework** (`staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/collector.go`):\\n   - `StableCollector` interface extends `prometheus.Collector` with stability awareness\\n   - `BaseStableCollector` provides a base implementation of custom collectors\\n   - Implements `Describe()` and `Collect()` methods that filter by registration state\\n   - Supports `DescribeWithStability()` and `CollectWithStability()` for custom metric hiding logic\\n\\n4. **HTTP Endpoint Registration** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/routes/metrics.go`):\\n   - `DefaultMetrics` struct implements route installation pattern\\n   - `Install()` method registers `/metrics` endpoint via `c.Handle(\\\"/metrics\\\", legacyregistry.Handler())`\\n   - Calls `register()` function that triggers metric registration in various subsystems:\\n     - `apimetrics.Register()` - API server metrics\\n     - `cachermetrics.Register()` - Storage cacher metrics\\n     - `etcd3metrics.Register()` - etcd3 backend metrics\\n     - `flowcontrolmetrics.Register()` - Flow control metrics\\n     - `peerproxymetrics.Register()` - Peer proxy metrics\\n     - `handlersmetrics.Register()` - Request handler metrics\\n\\n5. **Modular Metric Registration** (`staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/prometheus/controllers/metrics.go`):\\n   - Each subsystem defines its own metrics in isolated packages\\n   - `Register()` function uses `sync.Once` to ensure one-time registration\\n   - Metrics are registered to `legacyregistry.MustRegister()` during init\\n   - Example: `controllerInstanceCount` gauge tracks running managed controllers\\n\\n6. **SLI Metrics** (`staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/prometheus/slis/routes.go`):\\n   - Separate `/metrics/slis` endpoint for Service Level Indicator metrics\\n   - Uses registry-based pattern via `metrics.HandlerFor(Registry, metrics.HandlerOpts{})`\\n   - Supports both standard and reset variants\\n\\n**Key Characteristics:**\\n- Stability-level tracking: ALPHA, BETA, STABLE with deprecation version support\\n- Version-aware registration ensures old metrics are hidden when deprecated\\n- Global `legacyregistry` provides centralized collection point\\n- Separation of concerns: metrics registered at package init time across subsystems\\n- Both `/metrics` (primary) and `/metrics/slis` (SLI-specific) endpoints\\n\\n### Grafana Metrics Infrastructure\\n\\n**Architecture Pattern:** Grafana uses a simpler, application-centric metrics system with explicit service injection and direct Prometheus client usage.\\n\\n**Core Components:**\\n\\n1. **Instrumentation Service** (`pkg/server/instrumentation_service.go`):\\n   - Standalone HTTP service running on separate port (default: `:3000`)\\n   - `instrumentationService` struct wraps an HTTP server\\n   - `newInstrumentationServer()` creates a minimal HTTP mux with single endpoint: `router.Handle(\\\"/metrics\\\", promhttp.Handler())`\\n   - Uses `promhttp.Handler()` directly without custom instrumentation\\n   - Lifecycle managed via `services.BasicService` with start/stop handlers\\n\\n2. **Metrics Declaration** (`pkg/infra/metrics/metrics.go`):\\n   - All metrics are declared as global variables with Prometheus types:\\n     - `MInstanceStart prometheus.Counter`\\n     - `MPageStatus *prometheus.CounterVec`\\n     - `MApiStatus *prometheus.CounterVec`\\n     - `MProxyStatus *prometheus.CounterVec`\\n     - Many others for alerts, dashboards, datasources, rendering, etc.\\n   - Metrics initialized in `init()` function with `prometheus.NewCounter()`, `prometheus.NewCounterVec()`, `prometheus.NewGauge()`, `prometheus.NewSummary()`, etc.\\n   - All metrics use `ExporterName = \\\"grafana\\\"` as namespace\\n   - `initMetricVars(reg prometheus.Registerer)` function calls `reg.MustRegister()` for all metrics\\n   - `SetBuildInformation(reg prometheus.Registerer, ...)` creates dynamic build info metrics\\n   - `SetEnvironmentInformation(reg prometheus.Registerer, ...)` creates environment info metrics\\n\\n3. **Metrics Service** (`pkg/infra/metrics/service.go`):\\n   - `ProvideService()` performs dependency injection setup\\n   - Calls `initMetricVars(reg)` and `initFrontendMetrics(reg)` to register all metrics\\n   - `InternalMetricsService` runs optional Graphite bridge for metric forwarding\\n   - `ProvideRegisterer()` returns `legacyregistry.Registerer()` - uses Kubernetes' legacy registry internally\\n   - `ProvideGatherer()` returns wrapped `multiRegistry` combining Kubernetes and Prometheus gatherers\\n   - `addPrefixWrapper` decorator ensures all non-prefixed metrics get \\\"grafana_\\\" prefix\\n   - `multiRegistry` combines multiple gatherers with duplicate detection\\n\\n4. **Custom Metric Utilities** (`pkg/infra/metrics/metricutil/utils.go`):\\n   - `NewCounterStartingAtZero()` - initializes counters with zero observation\\n   - `NewCounterVecStartingAtZero()` - initializes counter vectors with all label combinations at zero\\n   - `buildLabelSets()` - generates Cartesian product of label values\\n   - Label name sanitization via `SanitizeLabelName()`\\n\\n5. **Frontend Metrics** (`pkg/infra/metrics/frontendmetrics.go`):\\n   - `initFrontendMetrics()` registers browser-side metric histograms\\n   - `registerFrontendHistogram()` pattern for consistent histogram registration\\n   - Maps metric names to recorder functions in `FrontendMetrics` map\\n   - Metrics include: boot load time, first paint, JS/CSS load timing\\n\\n6. **Dependency Injection** (`pkg/infra/metrics/wireset.go`):\\n   - Uses Google `wire` framework for DI\\n   - `WireSet` provides: ProvideService, ProvideRegisterer, ProvideGatherer\\n   - `WireSetForTest` provides test variants with fresh registries\\n\\n**Key Characteristics:**\\n- Simple, flat metrics structure with global variables\\n- Direct use of `prometheus.NewCounter()` family without custom wrappers\\n- Single `/metrics` endpoint via standard `promhttp.Handler()`\\n- Dependency injection via `wire` framework\\n- Automatic prefix wrapping via `addPrefixWrapper`\\n- Reuses Kubernetes' `legacyregistry` for underlying registry\\n- Explicit metric initialization in `init()` blocks and service providers\\n\\n### Comparison Summary\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | Grafana |\\n|--------|-----------|----------|\\n| **Registry Model** | Custom `KubeRegistry` with version/stability awareness | Direct Prometheus registry (with Kubernetes' legacyregistry underneath) |\\n| **Metric Declaration** | Lazy initialization in package init; uses `Registerable` interface | Global variables initialized in `init()` function |\\n| **Registration Mechanism** | Pluggable `Register()` functions across subsystems; called at route install time | Centralized in `initMetricVars()` and `initFrontendMetrics()` |\\n| **Deprecation Support** | Built-in: stability levels, version hiding, hidden metrics tracking | Not implemented; all metrics are permanent |\\n| **Collector Pattern** | Custom `StableCollector` base class for complex collectors | Direct prometheus.Collector usage via library |\\n| **HTTP Endpoint** | `/metrics` (main) + `/metrics/slis` (SLI-specific) | Single `/metrics` via `promhttp.Handler()` |\\n| **Instrumentation** | Auto-instrumented via `promhttp.InstrumentMetricHandler()` | Default promhttp instrumentation |\\n| **Metric Prefix** | Subsystem-specific; explicitly set in metric options | Automatic \\\"grafana_\\\" prefix wrapper |\\n| **Service Architecture** | Routes installed into existing API mux | Separate HTTP service on dedicated port |\\n| **Dependency Injection** | Package-level registration functions | Google `wire` framework with providers |\\n\\n### Exposition Pattern Summary\\n\\n**Kubernetes Pattern:**\\n1. Multiple subsystems register metrics via `Register()` functions called during route installation\\n2. Metrics collected by global `defaultRegistry` with stability/deprecation awareness\\n3. HTTP handler created via `promhttp.InstrumentMetricHandler()` wrapping `promhttp.HandlerFor()`\\n4. Supports custom collector frameworks via `StableCollector` interface\\n5. Designed for API server and cluster component monitoring\\n\\n**Grafana Pattern:**\\n1. All metrics declared globally and initialized in `init()` blocks\\n2. Metrics registered during service startup via `initMetricVars()` and `initFrontendMetrics()`\\n3. HTTP handler via standard `promhttp.Handler()` in isolated service\\n4. Metrics wrapped with automatic \\\"grafana_\\\" prefix for consistency\\n5. Simplified for application monitoring without version/deprecation complexity\"\n}\n",

(`pkg/infra/metrics/wireset.go`):\\n   - Uses Google `wire` framework for DI\\n   - `WireSet` provides: ProvideService, ProvideRegisterer, ProvideGatherer\\n   - `WireSetForTest` provides test variants with fresh registries\\n\\n**Key Characteristics:**\\n- Simple, flat metrics structure with global variables\\n- Direct use of `prometheus.NewCounter()` family without custom wrappers\\n- Single `/metrics` endpoint via standard `promhttp.Handler()`\\n- Dependency injection via `wire` framework\\n- Automatic prefix wrapping via `addPrefixWrapper`\\n- Reuses Kubernetes' `legacyregistry` for underlying registry\\n- Explicit metric initialization in `init()` blocks and service providers\\n\\n### Comparison Summary\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | Grafana |\\n|--------|-----------|----------|\\n| **Registry Model** | Custom `KubeRegistry` with version/stability awareness | Direct Prometheus registry (with Kubernetes' legacyregistry underneath) |\\n| **Metric Declaration** | Lazy initialization in package init; uses `Registerable` interface | Global variables initialized in `init()` function |\\n| **Registration Mechanism** | Pluggable `Register()` functions across subsystems; called at route install time | Centralized in `initMetricVars()` and `initFrontendMetrics()` |\\n| **Deprecation Support** | Built-in: stability levels, version hiding, hidden metrics tracking | Not implemented; all metrics are permanent |\\n| **Collector Pattern** | Custom `StableCollector` base class for complex collectors | Direct prometheus.Collector usage via library |\\n| **HTTP Endpoint** | `/metrics` (main) + `/metrics/slis` (SLI-specific) | Single `/metrics` via `promhttp.Handler()` |\\n| **Instrumentation** | Auto-instrumented via `promhttp.InstrumentMetricHandler()` | Default promhttp instrumentation |\\n| **Metric Prefix** | Subsystem-specific; explicitly set in metric options | Automatic \\\"grafana_\\\" prefix wrapper |\\n| **Service Architecture** | Routes installed into existing API mux | Separate HTTP service on dedicated port |\\n| **Dependency Injection** | Package-level registration functions | Google `wire` framework with providers |\\n\\n### Exposition Pattern Summary\\n\\n**Kubernetes Pattern:**\\n1. Multiple subsystems register metrics via `Register()` functions called during route installation\\n2. Metrics collected by global `defaultRegistry` with stability/deprecation awareness\\n3. HTTP handler created via `promhttp.InstrumentMetricHandler()` wrapping `promhttp.HandlerFor()`\\n4. Supports custom collector frameworks via `StableCollector` interface\\n5. Designed for API server and cluster component monitoring\\n\\n**Grafana Pattern:**\\n1. All metrics declared globally and initialized in `init()` blocks\\n2. Metrics registered during service startup via `initMetricVars()` and `initFrontendMetrics()`\\n3. HTTP handler via standard `promhttp.Handler()` in isolated service\\n4. Metrics wrapped with automatic \\\"grafana_\\\" prefix for consistency\\n5. Simplified for application monitoring without version/deprecation complexity\"\n}\n",
